<p><b>Franklin Edmundo Rijkaard</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˈfrɑŋk ˈrɛi̯kaːrt]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Frank_Rijkaard.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Nl-Frank_Rijkaard.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Frank Rijkaard.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; born 30 September 1962) is a Dutch former <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> and former manager who played as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">defender</a>. Rijkaard has played for <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a> and <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> and represented the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a> side 73 times, scoring 10 goals. In his managerial career, he has been at the helm of the Netherlands national team, <a href="/wiki/Sparta_Rotterdam" title="Sparta Rotterdam">Sparta Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_football_team" title="Saudi Arabia national football team">Saudi Arabia national team</a>.
</p><p>Regarded as one of the best defensive midfielders in footballing history and as one of the best players of his generation,<sup id="cite_ref-Dutchman_who_ruled_Europe_in_three_shirts_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutchman_who_ruled_Europe_in_three_shirts-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Frank_Rijkaard_Biography_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frank_Rijkaard_Biography-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> in 2010 Rijkaard was described by British broadsheet <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> as having been "a stylish player of faultless pedigree".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler,_nr._15a_F._Rijka,_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg/170px-Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg/255px-Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg/340px-Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler%2C_nr._15a_F._Rijka%2C_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2443" data-file-height="3656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ajax_selectie_seizoen_1981_1982_nr._140a_E._Ophof_speler,_nr._15a_F._Rijka,_Bestanddeelnr_253-8568.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rijkaard with Ajax in 1981</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ajax">Ajax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ajax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rijkaard was born in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>. His mother Neel is <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and his father <a href="/wiki/Herman_Rijkaard" title="Herman Rijkaard">Herman</a> (1935–2010)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> was a <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Surinamese</a> footballer who arrived in the Netherlands along with the father of <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a>; the two sons grew up playing together in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Rijkaard_finally_gets_frank_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rijkaard_finally_gets_frank-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Rijkaard was just 17 when <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Leo_Beenhakker" title="Leo Beenhakker">Leo Beenhakker</a> gave him his senior squad debut on 23 August 1980. He made an immediate impact, scoring the third goal in a 4–2 away victory over <a href="/wiki/Go_Ahead_Eagles" title="Go Ahead Eagles">Go Ahead Eagles</a>, the first league match in the <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Eredivisie" title="1980–81 Eredivisie">1980–81</a> season. He would play another 23 games for Ajax in his first season, netting four goals. In <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Eredivisie" title="1981–82 Eredivisie">1981–82</a>, he won his first league championship with Ajax and went on to successfully defend the title the following season.
</p><p>Rijkaard stayed at Ajax for seven-and-a-half seasons. During this period, he won the Dutch league championship three times (<a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Eredivisie" title="1981–82 Eredivisie">1981–82</a>, <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Eredivisie" title="1982–83 Eredivisie">1982–83</a>, <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Eredivisie" title="1984–85 Eredivisie">1984–85</a>) and the Dutch Cup three times (<a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_KNVB_Cup" title="1982–83 KNVB Cup">1982–83</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_KNVB_Cup" title="1985–86 KNVB Cup">1985–86</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_KNVB_Cup" title="1986–87 KNVB Cup">1986–87</a>). In the <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Eredivisie" title="1986–87 Eredivisie">1986–87</a> season, he won the <a href="/wiki/Cup_Winners%27_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Cup Winners&#39; Cup">Cup Winners' Cup</a> with Ajax over <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Leipzig" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokomotiv Leipzig">Lokomotiv Leipzig</a>, winning 1–0. In September 1987, what would have been Rijkaard's third season (<a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Eredivisie" title="1987–88 Eredivisie">1987–88</a>) under Dutchman <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a> as head coach, Rijkaard stormed off the training field and vowed never to play under him again. He was subsequently signed by <a href="/wiki/Sporting_CP" title="Sporting CP">Sporting CP</a>, but he signed too late to be eligible to play in any competition. He was immediately loaned out to <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a>, but upon completing his first season at Zaragoza was signed by <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A.C._Milan">A.C. Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: A.C. Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rijkaard played for five seasons at Milan. It was coach <a href="/wiki/Arrigo_Sacchi" title="Arrigo Sacchi">Arrigo Sacchi</a> who saw Rijkaard as playing a pivotal role at Milan and transformed the central defender into a world class holding midfielder, where the Dutchman's aggressive and firm style would go on to influence the likes of <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Vieira" title="Patrick Vieira">Patrick Vieira</a> to replicate in future years. Playing alongside fellow country-men <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a>, Rijkaard won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> twice (in <a href="/wiki/1989_European_Cup_Final" title="1989 European Cup Final">1989</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_European_Cup_Final" title="1990 European Cup Final">1990</a>, against <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a>) and the domestic <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> championship twice. In the 1990 European Cup Final, he scored the only goal to win the cup for Milan.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Ajax">Return to Ajax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Return to Ajax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After five seasons in Italy, Rijkaard returned to Ajax in 1993. With <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> at the helm, Rijkaard and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Blind" title="Danny Blind">Danny Blind</a> formed the experienced defensive core of the Ajax team that won the first two of three consecutive Dutch championships. Ajax were the unbeaten champions of the Netherlands in the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Eredivisie" title="1994–95 Eredivisie">1994–95</a> season, and carried that success into Europe. In his final game, Rijkaard won the Champions League with a 1–0 victory over Milan in the <a href="/wiki/1995_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1995 UEFA Champions League Final">1995 final</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ernst-Happel-Stadion" title="Ernst-Happel-Stadion">Ernst-Happel-Stadion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. He was named in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">FIFA 100</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a>'s list of the 125 World's Greatest Footballers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg/220px-Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg/330px-Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg/440px-Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2584" data-file-height="2349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frank_Rijkaard_and_Carmen_Sandries_1985.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frank Rijkaard and Carmen Sandries getting married on 10 October 1985</div></div></div>
<p>On the international stage, Rijkaard made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> in 1981. He was part of the Dutch side that won <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">UEFA Euro 1988</a> with a 2–0 win in the final over the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a>, playing at centre-back alongside <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a>. He won a total of 73 caps and scored 10 goals. Rijkaard also played for the Netherlands during the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a> and <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1992" title="UEFA Euro 1992">Euro 1992</a>.
</p><p>At Euro 1992, Rijkaard scored a late equalizer for the Netherlands in a 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> at the semi-final stage but the Dutch went out on penalties. He made his final appearance for the Netherlands in the 3–2 defeat against eventual winners <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in the quarter-finals of the 1994 World Cup.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spitting_incident">Spitting incident</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Spitting incident">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeist,_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.,_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg/220px-Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg/330px-Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg/440px-Zeist%2C_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.%2C_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3690" data-file-height="2462" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zeist,_training_Nederlands_elftal_in_verband_met_interland_tegen_Malta_v.l.n.r.,_Bestanddeelnr_932-8072.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rijkaard (left), with Ronald Koeman (third from right), <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Koeman" title="Erwin Koeman">Erwin Koeman</a> (second from right) and Ruud Gullit (right) in the Dutch national team in 1983</div></div></div>
<p>Rijkaard was the cause of an incident with <a href="/wiki/Rudi_V%C3%B6ller" title="Rudi Völler">Rudi Völler</a> when <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a> played the Netherlands in the 1990 World Cup. Rijkaard was booked for a tackle on Völler and, as Rijkaard took up position for the free kick, he spat in Völler's hair. Völler complained to the referee and was booked as well. From the resulting free kick, Völler then handled the ball and then went to the ground (according to his own account) to avoid a collision with Dutch keeper <a href="/wiki/Hans_van_Breukelen" title="Hans van Breukelen">Hans van Breukelen</a>, while others, notably Rijkaard and van Breukelen, saw Voller's handball and his resulting action as a dive in hopes for a penalty. Van Breukelen was angry at this but Rijkaard, already annoyed by Völler's previous antics, again confronted the West German by twisting his ear and stamping on his foot. Argentine referee <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Loustau" title="Juan Carlos Loustau">Juan Carlos Loustau</a> was tired of both Völler and Rijkaard's consistently hostile antics towards each other in such a short period of time, and fearing a fight between the two, sent off both Rijkaard and Völler. As he jogged back to the entrance tunnel, Rijkaard again spat in Völler's hair as they left the pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The German press nicknamed him "<a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">Llama</a>" for his spitting. Rijkaard would later apologise for his behaviour to Völler, who accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Regarded as one of the greatest players in his position, Rijkaard was a quick, strong, complete and tenacious defensive midfielder who was praised by pundits throughout his career for his physical and athletic attributes, his work rate, positioning, his acute tactical intelligence and decision-making, as well as his outstanding consistency and ability to read the game. Due to his aggression and versatility, he was also capable of playing as a <a href="/wiki/Central_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Central midfielder">central</a> or <a href="/wiki/Box-to-box_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Box-to-box midfielder">box-to-box midfielder</a>, and even in a <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">defensive</a> role, usually in the centre.<sup id="cite_ref-A.C._Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Frank_Rijkaard_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A.C._Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Frank_Rijkaard-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Although Rijkaard was known as strong tackler, he was surprisingly elegant for a player of his size, and also possessed good technique, passing ability, link-up play, and vision, which made him adept at starting attacking plays as a <a href="/wiki/Deep-lying_playmaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep-lying playmaker">deep-lying playmaker</a> once he won back possession;<sup id="cite_ref-A.C._Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Frank_Rijkaard_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A.C._Milan_Hall_of_Fame:_Frank_Rijkaard-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> because of his technical skills and creative abilities, he was also capable of playing in more advanced roles, as an <a href="/wiki/Attacking_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Attacking midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> or <a href="/wiki/Second_striker" class="mw-redirect" title="Second striker">second striker</a>. Due to his height and physical strength, he excelled in the air, and also possessed a powerful shot; furthermore, he was capable of getting forward and contributing to his team's attacking plays with goals by making late runs into the penalty area.<sup id="cite_ref-Dutchman_who_ruled_Europe_in_three_shirts_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dutchman_who_ruled_Europe_in_three_shirts-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Frank_Rijkaard_Biography_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frank_Rijkaard_Biography-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-magliarossonera_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-magliarossonera-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Managerial career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rijkaard's coaching career began when he was appointed manager of the Netherlands national team in 1998. He had previously served as an assistant coach, along with <a href="/wiki/Johan_Neeskens" title="Johan Neeskens">Johan Neeskens</a> and Ronald Koeman under the managerial tenure of <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a>. At the time, he was not taken seriously as a manager because of his inexperience, but he was able to guide his national side to the semi-finals of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a>. During the group phase, the Dutch team won slowly but surely and managed to get three victories: 1–0 against the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a>, 3–0 against Denmark and 3–2 against <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>. In the quarter-final, his side produced the biggest win of the competition, a 6–1 result against <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia</a>. The Netherlands played some of the best football of the tournament, but lost their semi-final match to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> on penalties; Rijkaard resigned immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Eredivisie" title="2001–02 Eredivisie">2001–02 season</a>, he became manager of <a href="/wiki/Sparta_Rotterdam" title="Sparta Rotterdam">Sparta Rotterdam</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a>, the oldest professional team in the country. Rijkaard enjoyed the down-to-earth atmosphere, although the club was not financially strong.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Under his leadership, the club was <a href="/wiki/Relegated" class="mw-redirect" title="Relegated">relegated</a> to the second division for the first time in its history, and he was consequently sacked.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Barcelona">Barcelona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Barcelona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_years">First years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: First years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rijkaard was not out of a coaching role for long, and less than a year after leaving Sparta, he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_FC_Barcelona_season" title="2003–04 FC Barcelona season">2003–04 season</a>. The season would prove to be a watershed for the club, but not without initial instability. Rijkaard arrived at the club as it entered a new phase, having elected a new president in <a href="/wiki/Joan_Laporta" title="Joan Laporta">Joan Laporta</a> and a new managerial board, but with fans unhappy that Laporta had let English midfielder <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> snub the chance to join the club. For Rijkaard, the team he inherited, with the exception of new superstar signing <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> (who was the club's second choice after Beckham), also consisted of many underachieving players from the old guard and era that failed to meet the club and its fans' demands to match archrival <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>'s success in the early 2000s, having not won a trophy since 1999.
</p><p>Rijkaard had a disappointing start at Barcelona that saw some sections of the club's fans call for his resignation, and he drew flak from the media when the team lost to Real Madrid in December 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Rijkaard's resilience won through and from 2004 onwards, he achieved a massive turnaround, as the team went from strength to strength. Barcelona finished runners-up in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> in <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_La_Liga" title="2003–04 La Liga">2003–04</a>, having been close to the relegation zone at one point in the earlier stages of the season. Rijkaard then took Barcelona to the next level as he  phased out the old guard and rebuilt a new-look side around Ronaldinho, with new players like <a href="/wiki/Deco" title="Deco">Deco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Eto%27o" title="Samuel Eto&#39;o">Samuel Eto'o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Rafael Márquez">Rafael Márquez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludovic_Giuly" title="Ludovic Giuly">Ludovic Giuly</a>, along with the latest promotion of some young players from the previous era trained in the club's youth teams, including <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Vald%C3%A9s" title="Víctor Valdés">Víctor Valdés</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Iniesta" title="Andrés Iniesta">Andrés Iniesta</a>. He eventually succeeded in turning around the fortunes of the club, with the strong support of Laporta, and within the next couple of years finally managed to win La Liga both in <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_La_Liga" title="2004–05 La Liga">2004–05</a> and in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_La_Liga" title="2005–06 La Liga">2005–06</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions_League_title_and_after">Champions League title and after</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Champions League title and after">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg/225px-FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg/338px-FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg/450px-FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2040" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_NASA_Jsc2006e33425.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rijkaard with <a href="/wiki/Xavi" title="Xavi">Xavi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carles_Puyol" title="Carles Puyol">Puyol</a> at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> in 2006.</div></div></div>
<p>Rijkaard became the first Barcelona coach to have won twice at Real Madrid's <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago Bernabéu Stadium">Santiago Bernabéu Stadium</a>, an achievement which even successful managers like Johan Cruyff, Louis van Gaal and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Aragon%C3%A9s" title="Luis Aragonés">Luis Aragonés</a> were unable to accomplish. His no-nonsense policy on and off the field, and the sparkling football played by his team, won him many plaudits and Rijkaard was among the five nominated coaches for <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>'s Team of the Year 2005. On 8 March 2006, he was also honoured by UEFA for his contributions to the European Cup competition throughout his career as player and manager.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rijkaard also achieved success on the European stage, winning the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2005–06 UEFA Champions League">2005–06 Champions League</a> with a <a href="/wiki/2006_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2006 UEFA Champions League Final">2–1</a> win against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the final. Barcelona had been losing 1–0 for most of the match before his late tactical substitutions proved the decisive factor, as the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Larsson" title="Henrik Larsson">Henrik Larsson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juliano_Belletti" title="Juliano Belletti">Juliano Belletti</a> contributed directly to Barcelona's two goals. The win made him the fifth individual to have won the European Cup both as a player and as a manager, alongside <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Mu%C3%B1oz" title="Miguel Muñoz">Miguel Muñoz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Trapattoni" title="Giovanni Trapattoni">Giovanni Trapattoni</a>, Johan Cruyff and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>, a feat later achieved also by his eventual successor, <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>.
</p><p>After losing to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">2007–08 Champions League</a>, Rijkaard was asked whether he would quit at the end of the season, since he had not won anything for two successive seasons. He replied, "I have no intention of leaving. It would be different if the players were saying it is time for me to go but that is not the case." On 1 May 2008, it was reported that Rijkaard allegedly confided to a colleague that he would be stepping down as Barcelona manager at the end of the season, but 24 hours later, he stated in a press conference that he had no intention of leaving the club.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 May 2008, the day after Barcelona's dismal 4–1 defeat to archrivals Real Madrid, Barcelona president Joan Laporta announced that at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_La_Liga" title="2007–08 La Liga">2007–08 season</a>, Rijkaard would no longer be head coach of the first team. Laporta made the announcement after a board meeting, and Rijkaard was succeeded by Pep Guardiola.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Laporta made it clear that Rijkaard's achievements "made history" and praised him for his time at the club.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galatasaray">Galatasaray</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Galatasaray">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 5 June 2009, Rijkaard signed a two-year contract to manage the Turkish <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="Süper Lig">Süper Lig</a> team <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a>, following the resignation of <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BClent_Korkmaz" title="Bülent Korkmaz">Bülent Korkmaz</a> two days earlier. He was sacked on 19 October 2010 and was replaced with <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Hagi" title="Gheorghe Hagi">Gheorghe Hagi</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 June 2011, it was announced that Rijkaard would be head coach of the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_football_team" title="Saudi Arabia national football team">Saudi Arabia national team</a> after a deal was reached with the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_Football_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi Arabia Football Federation">Saudi Arabia Football Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Saudi Arabia were eliminated in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_AFC_Third_Round" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – AFC Third Round">third round</a> of <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification">2014 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> after a 4–2 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a> in their last match on 29 February, finishing third in their group.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/21st_Arabian_Gulf_Cup" title="21st Arabian Gulf Cup">21st Arabian Gulf Cup</a> was the second competition for Rijkaard with Saudi Arabia. The Saudis left the competition at the group stage after losing 2–0 against <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">Iraq</a>, a 2–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Yemen_national_football_team" title="Yemen national football team">Yemen</a> and 1–0 defeat against <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">Kuwait</a>. On 16 January 2013, Rijkaard was dismissed under a confidential contractual termination penalty clause following Saudi Arabia's exit at the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montverde_Academy">Montverde Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Montverde Academy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> prep school <a href="/wiki/Montverde_Academy" title="Montverde Academy">Montverde Academy</a> hired Rijkaard as their advisor of player development.<sup id="cite_ref-montverde_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-montverde-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2016, Rijkaard announced he would no longer pursue a position as manager.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaching_philosophy_and_style">Coaching philosophy and style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Coaching philosophy and style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG/170px-Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG/255px-Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG/340px-Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="1366" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Galatasaray-Frank_Rijkaard.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rijkaard coaching Galatasaray in 2009.</div></div></div>
<p>As a coach, Rijkaard's essential philosophy is to guide his team towards playing attack-minded football as a cohesive unit. In doing this, he believes a team can achieve the dual objectives of winning games and ensuring the audience's enjoyment of the spectacle. This follows in the best coaching traditions of Rijkaard's countrymen and forebears <a href="/wiki/Rinus_Michels" title="Rinus Michels">Rinus Michels</a> and Johan Cruyff. In this light, it is notable that Michels coached both Cruyff and Rijkaard during their respective participations with the Dutch national team, and that Cruyff himself went on to coach Rijkaard. Nonetheless, Rijkaard believes in working within a contemporary football context and is not out to imitate the styles and tactics of past masters. In his own words: 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><i>you gain many impressions from the past. You still have it in your mind when you become a coach, and if something happens you can recall how it was dealt with. But I strongly believe that you cannot copy anyone. The decisions that a great coach made years ago will not necessarily work today.</i><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>Rijkaard has evidently learned to curb the quick temper of his playing days and is often a portrait of calm and stability in training and along the touchline. He rarely courts controversy in the media and is more apt now to promote a positive environment and let his team's play speak for itself when faced with intense rivalry or criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The tactics used during his tenure as manager of Barcelona best exemplify Rijkaard's commitment to playing stylish attacking football. During the team's 2004–05 and 2005–06 campaigns, the coach frequently fielded a <a href="/wiki/Formation_(association_football)" title="Formation (association football)">4–3–3</a> formation, a system which encouraged the flair and creativity of the players in the front third of the field and created optimal interplay between the midfielders and forwards during attacks, with Ronaldinho being the focal point of the team's offence.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Within this system, the four defenders also tended to play in a relatively high position on the pitch to support the midfield, which frequently advanced to participate in the attack. The team generally focuses on maintaining possession in the opponents' half of the field, applying pressure in order to force the opposition to make errors in defense and offensive counter-attacking.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rijkaard comes from a football-playing family. He is the son of <a href="/wiki/Herman_Rijkaard" title="Herman Rijkaard">Herman Rijkaard</a>, a former footballer who played for <a href="/wiki/SV_Robinhood" class="mw-redirect" title="SV Robinhood">SV Robinhood</a> in the Surinamese <a href="/wiki/SVB_Topklasse" title="SVB Topklasse">Hoofdklasse</a>, before emigrating to the Netherlands, where he played in the Dutch Eredivisie for <a href="/wiki/Blauw-Wit_Amsterdam" title="Blauw-Wit Amsterdam">FC Blauw-Wit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rijkaard_finally_gets_frank_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rijkaard_finally_gets_frank-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> His older brother, Herman Rijkaard, Jr., is a <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> certified players' agent who represents various players internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Twice divorced, he is currently married to Stephanie and has four children.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rijkaard features in <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a>' <i>FIFA</i> video game series; he was featured in the <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_14" title="FIFA 14">FIFA 14</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_15" title="FIFA 15">FIFA 15</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_16" title="FIFA 16">FIFA 16</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_17" title="FIFA 17">FIFA 17</a></i> Ultimate Team Legends.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/FIFA_18" title="FIFA 18">FIFA 18</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA_19" title="FIFA 19">FIFA 19</a>, he appeared as an ICON player in <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ultimate_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA Ultimate Team">FIFA Ultimate Team</a> (FUT).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_2">Player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frank_Rijkaard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><a href="/wiki/KNVB_Cup" title="KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup</a>: <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_KNVB_Cup" title="1982–83 KNVB Cup">1982–83</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_KNVB_Cup" title="1985–86 KNVB Cup">1985–86</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_KNVB_Cup" title="1986–87 KNVB Cup">1986–87</a></li>
